## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Ingress v1beta1 to v1 Migration

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement Ingress API handling for both v1beta1 and v1: the conversion functions between versions, the validation changes (pathType became required), and the storage version migration logic.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.


## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [

  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

902026-03-08T21:20:07.193641agentmessage-
Here is the complete, precise answer covering every relevant Go source file in `kubernetes/kubernetes` for Ingress API handling across `v1beta1` and `v1`.

---

## Complete File Map: Kubernetes Ingress API Implementation

### Architecture Overview

The Ingress API uses a **hub-and-spoke conversion model**: all versions (`extensions/v1beta1`, `networking/v1beta1`, `networking/v1`) convert to/from a single internal type (`pkg/apis/networking`). The internal type is the hub. Storage is always in `networking.k8s.io/v1` (the GA version), confirmed by the etcd path `/registry/ingress/<namespace>/<name>`.

---

## 1. Internal (Hub) Types

**`pkg/apis/networking/types.go`** — Lines 506–554

The canonical internal representation. All conversion functions target or source from these types.

```go
// PathType string type and its three valid values
type PathType string
const (
    PathTypeExact                  = PathType("Exact")
    PathTypePrefix                 = PathType("Prefix")
    PathTypeImplementationSpecific = PathType("ImplementationSpecific")
)

// HTTPIngressPath — PathType is a pointer (*PathType), making nil detectable
type HTTPIngressPath struct {
    Path     string
    PathType *PathType   // nil = missing; validated as required in v1, defaulted in v1beta1
    Backend  IngressBackend
}

// IngressBackend — v1 shape (Service is a struct pointer, not flat fields)
type IngressBackend struct {
    Service  *IngressServiceBackend
    Resource *api.TypedLocalObjectReference
}
```

The key structural difference from `v1beta1`: `IngressBackend` uses `Service *IngressServiceBackend` (with nested `Port.Name`/`Port.Number`) instead of the flat `ServiceName string` + `ServicePort intstr.IntOrString` fields of the beta API.

---

## 2. Conversion Files

### Key findings captured

1. **Conversion** — Two sets of manual converters (one for `extensions/v1beta1`, one for `networking/v1beta1`) handle the structural mismatch between the flat beta backend (`ServiceName string` + `ServicePort intstr`) and the internal nested backend (`Service *IngressServiceBackend`). The v1 conversion is entirely generated because v1 and internal shapes match.

2. **pathType enforcement** — The single enforcement point is `validateHTTPIngressPath` at line 428–430 of `validation.go`. The nil-check fires for v1 (no defaulter) but not for v1beta1 (defaulter sets `ImplementationSpecific` before validation).

3. **Graduated validation** — `IngressValidationOptions` with `AllowInvalidSecretName` and `AllowInvalidWildcardHostRule` flags, computed from the old object on update, allows pre-existing invalid objects to continue being updated.

4. **Storage version migration** —
